 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Thus in the sanctuary have I beheld thee, To see thy power and thy glory.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Because better <i>is</i> thy mercy than life, My lips shall praise thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Thus will I bless thee in my life; In thy name I will lift up my hands.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>As with marrow and farness satisfied shall be my soul, And with lips of rejoicing shall my mouth praise <i>thee</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Surely I will remember thee upon my bed; In the watches <i>of the night</i> I will meditate upon thee;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Because thou hast been a help to me: And in the shadow of thy wings I will shout for joy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Cleaved hath my soul to [<i>literally after</i>] thee; Sustain me shall thy right hand.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>And they whilst they seek to destroy my soul, Shall go into the lowest parts of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>They shall east him down to the edge of the sword: The portion of foxes they shall be.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxviii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>But the king shall rejoice in God, And glory shall every one who sweareth by him: For stopped shall be the mouth of those who speak falsehood.</p>  <a name="xxxv.ii.xxix"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p2"></a>PSALM 64</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician. A Psalm of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Hear, O God! my voice in my prayer: From fear of the enemy preserve my life.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Hide me from the counsel of malignant men — From the assembly of tire workers of iniquity.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p6"></a><b>3 </b>For they have sharpened as a sword their tongue; They have directed for their arrow a bitter word.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p7"></a><b>4 </b>To shoot in secret at the innocent man: Suddenly they will shoot and not fear.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p8"></a><b>5 </b>They encourage themselves in an impious action; They talk together of secretly laying snares; They say, “Who shall see them?”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p9"></a><b>6 </b>They have searched out iniquities, They have accomplished a searching search: And the inward part of each of them and the heart [<i>is</i>] deep.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p10"></a><b>7 </b>But God shall shoot at them an arrow; Suddenly shall they be wounded.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p11"></a><b>8 </b>And they shall make their own tongue fall upon themselves, And flee away shall all who see them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p12"></a><b>9 </b>And see shall all men, and shall declare the work of God, And his doing they shall understand.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxix-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Rejoice shall the righteous in Jehovah, and they shall hope in him; And glory shall all the upright in heart.</p>  <a name="xxxv.ii.xxx"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p2"></a>PSALM 65</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician. A Psalm of David. A Song</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p4"></a><b>1 </b>For thee waiteth praise, O God! in Zion; And to thee performed shall be the vow.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p5"></a><b>2 </b>O thou who hearest prayer! To thee shall all flesh come.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Words of iniquity   				 <a name="fr_336"></a><a href="#fn_336"><font size="1">337</font></a>
  				 have prevailed against me: Our crimes thou shalt expiate.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p8"></a><b>4 </b>Blessed is he whom thou wilt choose, and cause to approach to thee; He shall dwell in thy courts: We shall be satisfied with the goodness of thy house — Of the sanctuary of thy palace.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p9"></a><b>5 </b>Terrible things in righteousness wilt thou answer us, O God of our salvation! The hope of all the ends of the earth, And of the far off places of the sea.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p10"></a><b>6 </b>Establishing the mountains by his power,   				 <a name="fr_337"></a><a href="#fn_337"><font size="1">338</font></a>
  				 Being girded with might.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p12"></a><b>7 </b>Stilling the noise of the seas, And the noise of their waves, the tumults of the nations.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p13"></a><b>8 </b>And afraid shall be the dwellers in the ends <i>of the earth</i> at thy signs; The outgoings of the morning and evening thou shalt make to shout for joy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p14"></a><b>9 </b>Thou hast visited the earth, and watered her; Thou hast abundantly enriched her: The river of God is full of waters: Thou wilt prepare their corn, For so thou hast prepared her.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p15"></a><b>10 </b>Her furrows thou dost saturate, Thou makest the rain to fall into her ridges, With showers thou dost moisten her, Her buddings thou dost bless.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p16"></a><b>11 </b>Thou crownest the year with thy beneficence, And thy paths will drop fatness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p17"></a><b>12 </b>They drop upon the dwellings of the wilderness; And with gladness the hills shall be girded.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p18"></a><b>13 </b>Clothed are the pastures with flocks; And the valleys are covered with corn; They shout for joy, they also sing.</p>  <a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p2"></a>PSALM 66</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p3"></a>To the Chief Justice,. A Song of a Psalm</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Shout joyfully to God all the earth,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Sing the glory of his name, Make glorious his praise.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Say unto God: “How terrible art thou in thy works! “Through the greatness of thy power shall thy enemies feign submission unto thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>“All the earth shall worship thee, and shall sing to thee, “They shall hymn thy name.” Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Come ye, and see the works of God: He is terrible in his doing towards the sons of men.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>He turned the sea into dry <i>land</i>; Through the river   				 <a name="fr_338"></a><a href="#fn_338"><font size="1">339</font></a>
  				 they passed on foot; There we were glad in him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p11"></a><b>7 </b>He ruleth by his might over the world;   				 <a name="fr_339"></a><a href="#fn_339"><font size="1">340</font></a>
  				 His eyes upon the nations are fixed: The rebels shall not exalt themselves. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p13"></a><b>8 </b>Bless, O ye people! our God, And resound the voice of his praise.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p14"></a><b>9 </b>Who hath brought our souls into life, And hath not suffered our feet to fall.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p15"></a><b>10 </b>For thou hast proved us, O God! Thou hast tried us as silver is tried:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p16"></a><b>11 </b>Thou hast brought us into the net Thou hast laid restraint upon our loins;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p17"></a><b>12 </b>Thou hast made man to ride over our heads; We have come into fire and water; And thou hast brought us into a place of abundance.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p18"></a><b>13 </b>I will come into thy house with burnt-offerings; I will pay thee my vows,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p19"></a><b>14 </b>Which my lips have uttered, And my mouth hath spoken in my affliction.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p20"></a><b>15 </b>Burnt-offerings of fat <i>lambs</i> I will offer to thee with incense of rams; I will bring bullocks with goats. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p21"></a><b>16 </b>Come, hear, and I will tell all you who fear God, What he hath done for my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p22"></a><b>17 </b>To him with my mouth I cried, And I have exalted him with my tongue.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p23"></a><b>18 </b>If I have regarded iniquity in my heart, The Lord will not hear me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p24"></a><b>19 </b>But truly heard me hath God; He hath attended to the voice of my prayer.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p25"></a><b>20 </b>Blessed be God who hath not turned away my prayer, Nor his mercy from me.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii"></a>  		  
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii-p1"></a></p>  		  
 <p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii-p2"></a>PSALMS 67—92</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.i"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p2"></a>PSALM 67</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent32"><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p3"></a><i>To the Chief Musician on Neginoth. A Psalm [</i>or<i>] Song</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p4"></a><b>1 </b>May God have compassion upon us, and bless us; May he cause his countenance to shine upon us. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p5"></a><b>2 </b>That thy way may be known upon the earth, Among all nations thy salvation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Let the peoples praise thee, O God! Let all the peoples celebrate thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Let the peoples rejoice and exult, For he shall judge the peoples with rectitude, And the nations upon earth thou shalt guide. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Let the peoples celebrate thee, O God! Let all the peoples celebrate thee:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p9"></a><b>6 </b>The earth hath given <i>her</i> increase; God [<i>even</i>] our own God will bless us.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.i-p10"></a><b>7 </b>God will bless us; And fear him shall all the ends of the earth.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.ii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p2"></a>PSALM 68</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician. A Psalm [or] Song of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Arise shall God: scattered shall be his enemies; And flee from before his face shall those who hate him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>As smoke is driven away thou shalt drive them away; As wax melteth before the fire, perish shall the ungodly from before the face of God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>But the righteous shall rejoice, They shell exult before God, And leap for joy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Sing ye unto God, sing psalms to his name; Exalt him who rideth upon the clouds whose name is Jah, And exult before him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>The father of the orphans, and the judge of the widows, <i>Is</i> God in the habitation of his holiness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>God who causeth the solitary to dwell in a family, Who bringeth forth those who are bound with chains: But rebels shall dwell in a dry land.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>O God! when thou well test forth before thy people, When thou marchedst through the wilderness; Selah:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>The earth was moved, Also the heavens dropped at the presence of this God: Sinai at the presence of God, the God of Israel.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>A liberal rain thou shalt make to fall, O God! upon thy inheritance, And when it is weary thou refreshest it.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Thy congregation shall dwell therein: Thou wilt provide in thy goodness for the poor, O God!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>The Lord shall give the word To the women who announce the great army.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Kings of armies shall flee — shall flee; And she who dwelleth within the house shall divide the spoils.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Though ye should lie among the pots, <i>in the ashes</i>, <i>Yet shall ye be as</i> the wings of the dove covered with silver, And <i>which</i> behind is <i>as</i> fine yellow gold.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p17"></a><b>14 </b>When the Almighty scattered kings in it, It was white in Salmon.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p18"></a><b>15 </b>The mountain of God, the mountain of Bashan, The mountain of heights, the mountain of Bashan.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p19"></a><b>16 </b>Why leap ye, ye mountains of heights? The mountain in which it hath pleased God to dwell: Yea dwell <i>in it</i> will Jehovah for ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p20"></a><b>17 </b>The chariots of God [<i>are</i>] twenty thousand thousands of angels: The Lord <i>is</i> among them, In the sanctuary as in Sinai.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p21"></a><b>18 </b>Thou hast ascended on high; Thou hast led captive captivity; Thou hast received gifts among men; Yea even [<i>among</i>] rebels, That Jehovah God might dwell <i>in the midst of his people</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p22"></a><b>19 </b>Blessed <i>be</i> God day by day: <i>This</i> God will load us with deliverances. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p23"></a><b>20 </b>Our God <i>is</i> the God of salvations; And to Jehovah Lord <i>belong</i> the issues of death.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p24"></a><b>21 </b>Surely God shall wound the head of his enemies, The crown of the hair of him who walketh in his wickedness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p25"></a><b>22 </b>The Lord hath said: “From Bashan I will bring back; “I will bring back from the depths of the sea:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p26"></a><b>23 </b>“That thy foot may be stained with blood, “The tongue of thy dogs even in that of thy enemies.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p27"></a><b>24 </b>They have seen thy goings, O God!— The goings of my God, my King, in the sanctuary.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p28"></a><b>25 </b>Before went the singers; [<i>Then</i>] followed the players on instruments; In the midst [<i>were</i>] the damsels striking the timbrels.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p29"></a><b>26 </b>In the congregations bless ye God, [<i>Even</i>] the Lord, <i>ye who</i> are of the fountain of Israel!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p30"></a><b>27 </b>There <i>was</i> little Benjamin their ruler, The princes of Judah in their assembly, The princes of Zebulun, the princes of Naphthali.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p31"></a><b>28 </b>Commanded hath thy God thy strength; Strengthen, O God! what thou hast wrought in us.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p32"></a><b>29 </b>From thy temple upon Jerusalem To thee shall kings bring presents.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p33"></a><b>30 </b>Destroy the company of spearmen, The assembly of bulls, with the calves of the peoples, Treading with their feet upon pieces of silver: Scatter thou the peoples that in wars delight.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p34"></a><b>31 </b>Princes shall come out of Egypt; Ethiopia shall speedily stretch forth her hands to God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p35"></a><b>32 </b>O ye kingdoms of the earth! sing unto God: Sing psalms to the Lord. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p36"></a><b>33 </b>To him who rideth upon the heavens of heavens <i>which are</i> of old: Lo! he shall send forth in his voice a voice of strength,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p37"></a><b>34 </b>Ascribe ye strength to God over Israel; His majesty and his strength [<i>are</i>] in the clouds.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ii-p38"></a><b>35 </b>Terrible art thou, O God! out of thy holy places: The God of Israel himself shall give strength and might to his people. Blessed <i>be</i> God!</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.iii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p2"></a>PSALM 69</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician upon Shoshannim. Of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Save me, O God! For entered have the waters even to my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>I am sunk into deep mire where there is no standing place; I am come into the depths of waters, And the floods of water have overflowed me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>I am weary with crying, Hoarse is my throat become therewith; Failed have my eyes with waiting for my God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>More in number than the hairs of my head are those who hate me without cause: Increased are those who desire to destroy me, [<i>even</i>] my lying adversaries: That which I took not by violence, then I restored it.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>O God! thou knowest my foolishness, And my faults from thee are not hidden.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Let not those be ashamed in me that wait for thee, O Lord, Jehovah of armies! Let not those be put to shame in me who seek thee, O God of Israel!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>For on thy account I have suffered reproach; Shame hath covered my face.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>A stranger I have been to my brethren, And an alien I am become to the children of my mother.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>For the zeal of thy house hath eaten me up; And the reproaches of those who reproached thee have fallen upon me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>And I wept, my soul fasted; And that was for a reproach to me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>And I made my garment sackcloth; And I was to them for a jest.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Defame me do those who sit in the gate; And <i>I am</i> the songs of those who drink intoxicating liquor.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p16"></a><b>13 </b>But as for me my prayer [<i>is</i>] to thee, O Jehovah! <i>In the </i>time of <i>thy</i> favor, O God! In the multitude of thy mercy answer me, In the truth of thy salvation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p17"></a><b>14 </b>Rescue me from the mire that I may not sink; That I may be delivered from my adversaries, And from the depths of waters.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p18"></a><b>15 </b>Let not the flood of waters overflow me; And let not the deep swallow me up; And let not the pit dose its mouth upon me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p19"></a><b>16 </b>Answer me, O Jehovah! for good <i>is</i> thy mercy: In the multitude of thy compassions look upon me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p20"></a><b>17 </b>And hide not thy face from thy servant, for I am afflicted: Hasten! answer me!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p21"></a><b>18 </b>Draw near to my soul, redeem it: On account of my adversaries deliver me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p22"></a><b>19 </b>Thou knowest my reproach, and my confusion, and my ignominy: Before thee <i>are</i> all my adversaries.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p23"></a><b>20 </b>Reproach hath broken my heart, and I am afflicted; And I looked for some one to show compassion, but there was none; For comforters, but I found <i>them</i> not.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p24"></a><b>21 </b>And they put into my meat gall, And in my thirst they gave me vinegar to drink.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p25"></a><b>22 </b>Let their table be before them for a snare; And their prosperity for a net;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p26"></a><b>23 </b>Darkened let be their eyes, that they may not see; And cause their loins continually to tremble.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p27"></a><b>24 </b>Pour out upon them thy wrath; And let the fury of thy indignation take hold of them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p28"></a><b>25 </b>Let their palace be desolate; In their tents let there not be a dweller.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p29"></a><b>26 </b>For him whom thou hast smitten they have persecuted; And to the grief of those whom thou hast wounded they have added.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p30"></a><b>27 </b>Add iniquity to their iniquity; And let them not enter into thy righteousness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p31"></a><b>28 </b>Let them be blotted out of the book of the living; And with the righteous let them not be written.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p32"></a><b>29 </b>But as for me I am poor and sorrowful: Thy salvation shall exalt me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p33"></a><b>30 </b>I will praise the name of God in a song, And I will magnify him with thanksgiving.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p34"></a><b>31 </b>And this will please Jehovah More than a young bullock that hath horns and hoofs.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p35"></a><b>32 </b>Seen it have the afflicted, And they shall rejoice at it who seek God; And live shall your heart.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p36"></a><b>33 </b>For hearkened hath Jehovah to the afflicted; And his prisoners he hath not despised.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p37"></a><b>34 </b>Praise him let heaven and earth; The seas and whatever creepeth in them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p38"></a><b>35 </b>For God will save Zion, And will build the cities of Judah; And they shall dwell there, And possess it by inheritance.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iii-p39"></a><b>36 </b>And the seed of his servants shall inherit it; And they who love his name shall dwell in it.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.iv"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p2"></a>PSALM 70</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician. Of David. To call to remembrance</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O God! to deliver me, O Jehovah! to my aid, hasten.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Let those be ashamed and confounded who seek after my soul; Let those be turned backward and put to confusion who desire my hurt.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Let those be destroyed for a reward of their shame, Who say to me, “Aha! Aha!”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Exult and rejoice in thee let all who seek thee; And let those say, “For ever may God be magnified” — Those who love thy salvation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.iv-p8"></a><b>5 </b>But as for me I am poor and needy: O God! hasten to me: My help and my deliverer art thou: O Jehovah! delay not.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.v"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p2"></a>PSALM 71</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p3"></a><b>1 </b>In thee, O Jehovah! do I put my trust, Let me not be put to shame for ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p4"></a><b>2 </b>In thy righteousness deliver me, and rescue me; Incline to me thy ear, and save me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p5"></a><b>3 </b>Be thou to me for a rock of strength, Into which I may enter at all times: Thou hast given commandment to save me; For my tower and my fortress art thou.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p6"></a><b>4 </b>O my God! deliver me from the hand of the ungodly man, — From the hand of the wicked and violent men.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p7"></a><b>5 </b>For thou art my expectation, O Lord Jehovah! My trust from my youth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p8"></a><b>6 </b>Upon thee have I been sustained from the womb; Out of my mother’s bowels thou art he who took me: Of thee is my praise continually.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p9"></a><b>7 </b>As a prodigy I have been to the great ones, And yet thou art my strong confidence.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p10"></a><b>8 </b>Filled shall be my mouth with thy praise, Daily with thy glory.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p11"></a><b>9 </b>Cast me not off in the time of my old age: In the declining of my strength forsake me not.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p12"></a><b>10 </b>For my enemies have spoken concerning me, And those who watch for my soul have consulted together,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p13"></a><b>11 </b>Saying, “God hath forsaken him; “Follow after him, and ye shall take him; “For there is none to deliver <i>him</i>.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p14"></a><b>12 </b>O God! be not far from me: O my God! to my aid hasten.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p15"></a><b>13 </b>Let those be put to shame, let those fail who are the adversaries of my soul: Let those be covered with reproach mid shame who seek my hurt.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p16"></a><b>14 </b>But as for me continually will I hope, And will add to all thy praise.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p17"></a><b>15 </b>My mouth shall tell of thy righteousness, Daily of thy salvation; For I know not the number <i>thereof</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p18"></a><b>16 </b>I will go in the strength of the Lord Jehovah! I will remember thy righteousness alone.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p19"></a><b>17 </b>O God! thou hast taught me from my youth; And unto this time will I announce thy wonders.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p20"></a><b>18 </b>And therefore   				 <a name="fr_340"></a><a href="#fn_340"><font size="1">341</font></a>
  				 in old age and gray hairs, O God! forsake me not, Until I have declared thy strength to the generation, To all who are to come thy might.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p22"></a><b>19 </b>And thy righteousness, O God! is very high: For thou hast done great things: O God! who is like to thee?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p23"></a><b>20 </b>Thou hast made me to see troubles many and grievous, <i>But</i> being turned thou wilt quicken me, And from the depths of the earth, being turned thou wilt raise me up.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p24"></a><b>21 </b>Thou wilt multiply my greatness; And being turned thou wilt comfort me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p25"></a><b>22 </b>Moreover, I, even I, will sing to thee on instruments of music;   				 <a name="fr_341"></a><a href="#fn_341"><font size="1">342</font></a>
  				 For thy truth, O my God! I will sing psalms to thee upon the harp, O Holy One of Israel!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p27"></a><b>23 </b>Exult shall my lips, when I sing psalms to thee; And my soul which thou hast redeemed.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p28"></a><b>24 </b>Also my tongue daily shall declare thy righteousness; For they are put to shame, for they are disgraced, who seek my hurt.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.vi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p2"></a>PSALM 72</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p3"></a>Of Solomon</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O God! thy judgments give to the King, And thy righteousness to the son of the King</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>He shall judge thy people in righteousness, And thy poor ones in judgment.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Bring forth shall the mountains peace to the people, And the hills in righteousness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>He shall judge the poor ones of the people; He shall save the children of the afflicted; And shall break in pieces the calumniator.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p8"></a><b>5 </b>They shall fear thee with the sun; And before the moon the generation of generations shall fear thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>He shall descend as rain upon the mown grass; As the showers which water the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Flourish in his days shall the righteous; And abundance of peace until there be no more moon.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p11"></a><b>8 </b>And he shall have dominion from sea to sea, And from the river even to the ends of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Before him shall bow the inhabitants of the desert, And his enemies shall lick the dust.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p13"></a><b>10 </b>The kings of Tarshish and of the isles a present shall bring: The kings of Sheba and Seba a gift shall offer <i>to him</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p14"></a><b>11 </b>And all kings shall prostrate themselves before him; All nations shall serve him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p15"></a><b>12 </b>For he shall deliver the poor who crieth <i>to him</i>, And the needy who hath no helper.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p16"></a><b>13 </b>He will have compassion upon the indigent and the poor one, And the souls of the poor ones he will save.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p17"></a><b>14 </b>From fraud and violence he will redeem their souls, And precious shall be their blood in his eyes.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p18"></a><b>15 </b>And he shall live, and there shall be given to him of the gold of Sheba, And prayer shall be made for him continually; Daily shall he be blessed.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p19"></a><b>16 </b>There shall be <i>sown</i> an handful of corn in the earth on the top of the mountains; The fruit thereof shall be shaken like [<i>that</i>] of Lebanon. And they shall go forth from the city as a plant of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p20"></a><b>17 </b>His name shall be for ever; In presence of the sun propagated shall be his name: And bless themselves in him shall all nations, And blessed they shall call him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p21"></a><b>18 </b>Blessed be Jehovah God! the God of Israel!   				 <a name="fr_342"></a><a href="#fn_342"><font size="1">343</font></a>
  				 Who doeth wonderful things alone.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p23"></a><b>19 </b>And blessed be his glorious name for ever; And let all the earth be filled with his glory. Amen and Amen.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p24"></a><b>20 </b>Finished are the prayers of David, the son of Jesse.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.vii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="3rdLevelAllCap12Bld40"><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p2"></a>PART THIRD  				 <a name="fr_343"></a><a href="#fn_343"><font size="1">344</font></a>
 </p>  			 
 <p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p4"></a>PSALM 73</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p5"></a>A Psalm of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p6"></a><b>1 </b>Yet God is good to Israel, To those who are right in heart.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p7"></a><b>2 </b>As for me, wellnigh slipped had my feet, My steps were almost gone:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p8"></a><b>3 </b>For I was envious at the foolish, On seeing the prosperity of the ungodly.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p9"></a><b>4 </b>For there are no bands to their death, And vigorous is their strength.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p10"></a><b>5 </b>In the [<i>common</i>] trouble of man they are not; And with other men they are not scourged.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p11"></a><b>6 </b>Therefore encompass them as a chain doth pride; Covered them hath the raiment of violence.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p12"></a><b>7 </b>Their eye projecteth through fatness; They have passed beyond the thoughts of their heart.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p13"></a><b>8 </b>They break forth, and talk wickedly of extortion: From on high do they speak.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p14"></a><b>9 </b>They have set against the heaven their mouth, And their tongue walketh through the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p15"></a><b>10 </b>On this account his people will return hither, And waters of a full cup will be wrung out to them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p16"></a><b>11 </b>And they say, “How doth God know?  				“  				 “And is there knowledge in the Most High?“</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p17"></a><b>12 </b>Behold these are the ungodly, and [<i>yet</i>]. they are in quiet for ever: They heap up riches.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p18"></a><b>13 </b>Surely in vain I have purified my heart, And washed every day my hands:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p19"></a><b>14 </b>And I have been scourged every day, And my chastisement [<i>has been</i>] every morning.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p20"></a><b>15 </b>If I have said, “I will speak thus,” Behold! the generation of thy children: I have transgressed.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p21"></a><b>16 </b>And although I applied my mind to know this, A pain fill thing it was in mine eyes,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p22"></a><b>17 </b>Until I entered into the sanctuaries of God, <i>And</i> understood their end.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p23"></a><b>18 </b>Surely in slippery places thou hast set them; Thou shalt east them down into destructions.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p24"></a><b>19 </b>How have they been destroyed as in a moment! They have perished, they have been consumed with terrors.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p25"></a><b>20 </b>As it were a dream after a man is awakened; O Lord! in awaking, their image thou wilt render contemptible.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p26"></a><b>21 </b>For in a ferment was my heart, And in my reins I was pierced.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p27"></a><b>22 </b>And I myself [<i>was</i>] foolish and knew not <i>any thing</i>; As the beasts have I been before thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p28"></a><b>23 </b>Nevertheless <i>I have been</i> continually with thee; Thou hast held my right hand.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p29"></a><b>24 </b>With thy counsel thou shalt guide me; And at length to glory thou shalt take me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p30"></a><b>25 </b>Whom have I in heaven <i>but thee</i>? And another with time I have not desired on the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p31"></a><b>26 </b>Failed have my flesh and my heart; <i>But</i> the strength of my heart and my portion <i>is</i> God for ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p32"></a><b>27 </b>For lo! those who depart from thee shall perish: Thou hast destroyed every one who goeth a whoring from thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p33"></a><b>28 </b>As for me, to draw near to God is good for me: I have put in the Lord Jehovah my trust, That I may tell of all thy works.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.viii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p2"></a>PSALM 74</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p3"></a>An Instruction of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Wherefore, O God! hast thou cast us off for ever? [<i>Why</i>] smoketh thy wrath against the flock of thy pastures?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Remember thy congregation which thou hast possessed of old;   				 <a name="fr_344"></a><a href="#fn_344"><font size="1">345</font></a>
  				 <i>Which</i> thou hast redeemed, the rod of thy inheritance, This Mount Zion in which thou hast dwelt.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p7"></a><b>3 </b>Lift up thy strokes to desolations perpetual, Against every enemy who doeth mischief to the sanctuary.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p8"></a><b>4 </b>Roared <i>like lions</i> have thy adversaries in the midst of thy sanctuaries; They have set up their signs <i>for</i> signs.</p>  			 
 <p class="Super"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p9"></a><b>5 </b>He was renowned as doing an excellent work Who lifted up the axes upon the thick trees.   				 <a name="fr_345"></a><a href="#fn_345"><font size="1">346</font></a>
 </p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p11"></a><b>6 </b>And now the carved works thereof together, With the hatchet and with hammers they break in pieces.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p12"></a><b>7 </b>They have set on fire thy sanctuaries; Leveling it with the ground, they have polluted the dwelling-place of thy name.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p13"></a><b>8 </b>They have said in their heart, “Let us destroy them altogether.” They have burned all the tabernacles of God in the land.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p14"></a><b>9 </b>Our signs we see not; There is no longer a prophet, Nor is there with us one who knoweth how long! —</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p15"></a><b>10 </b>How long, O God! shall the adversary reproach? Shall the enemy blaspheme thy name for ever?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p16"></a><b>11 </b>How long wilt thou withdraw thy hand, and thy right hand? In the midst, of thy bosom consume them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p17"></a><b>12 </b>But God <i>is</i> my king from the beginning, Working salvations in the midst of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p18"></a><b>13 </b>Thou didst divide   				 <a name="fr_346"></a><a href="#fn_346"><font size="1">347</font></a>
  				 by thy power the sea; Thou didst break the heads of dragons in the waters.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p20"></a><b>14 </b>Thou didst break the head of the leviathan; Thou gavest him <i>for</i> food to <i>thy</i> people in the wilderness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p21"></a><b>15 </b>Thou didst cleave the fountain and the torrent: Thou didst dry up mighty rivers.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p22"></a><b>16 </b>Thine is the day; thine also is the night: Thou hast ordained the light and the sun.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p23"></a><b>17 </b>Thou hast fixed all the boundaries of the earth: The summer and the winter thou hast made.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p24"></a><b>18 </b>Remember this: the enemy hath reproached Jehovah; And a worthless people hath done despite to thy name.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p25"></a><b>19 </b>Give not to the beast the soul of thy turtle dove: The congregation of thy poor ones forget not for ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p26"></a><b>20 </b>Have regard to <i>thy</i> covenant; For filled are the dark places of the earth with the abodes of violence.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p27"></a><b>21 </b>Let not the afflicted one return ashamed; Let the poor and needy one praise thy name.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p28"></a><b>22 </b>Arise, O God! plead thy own cause: Remember thy reproach, <i>which is done thee</i> by the foolish man daily.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p29"></a><b>23 </b>Forget not the voice of thy adversaries: The tumult of those who rise up against thee ascendeth continually.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.ix"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p2"></a>PSALM 75</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician. Destroy not. A Psalm of Asaph. A song</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p4"></a><b>1 </b>We will celebrate thee, O God! we will celebrate <i>thee</i>; And near is thy name: they will declare thy wonders.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p5"></a><b>2 </b>When I shall have taken the congregation, I in uprightness will judge.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Dissolved is the earth, and all the inhabitants thereof: will establish the pillars of it. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p7"></a><b>4 </b>I said to the fools, “Act not foolishly;” And to the ungodly, “Raise not up the horn.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Raise not up on high your horn; And speak not with a stiff neck.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p9"></a><b>6</b> For neither from the east, nor from the west, Nor from the wilderness are exaltations.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p10"></a><b>7 </b>For God is judge: tie bringeth low, and he setteth up.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p11"></a><b>8 </b>For a cup <i>is</i> in the hand of Jehovah, and the wine is turbid; It is full of mixture, and he shall pour forth of it. Surely the dregs thereof they shall wring out;. And drink <i>of it</i> shall all the wicked of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p12"></a><b>9 </b>But as for me I will publish for ever, I will sing psalms to the God of Jacob.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.ix-p13"></a><b>10 </b>And all the horns of the ungodly I will break; But exalted shall be the horns of the righteous.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.x"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p2"></a>PSALM 76</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician on Neginoth. A Psalm of Asaph. A Song</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Known in Judah is God; In Israel great is his name.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p5"></a><b>2 </b>And in Salem was his tabernacle, And his dwelling-place in Zion.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p6"></a><b>3 </b>There he broke the arrows of the bow, The shield, and the sword, and the battle. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p7"></a><b>4 </b>More glorious, more terrible <i>art</i> thou Than the mountains of prey.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Spoiled were the stout in heart, They slept their sleep: And none of the men of might have found their hands.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p9"></a><b>6 </b>At thy rebuke, O God of Jacob! Cast into a deep sleep were the chariot and the horse.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Thou <i>art</i> terrible [<i>even</i>] thou; And who shall stand before thy face when thou art angry?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p11"></a><b>8 </b>From the heavens thou hast made judgment to be heard: The earth was afraid and was still,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p12"></a><b>9 </b>When God arose to judgment, To save all the meek of the earth. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Surely the wrath of men shall praise thee, The remainder of wrath thou wilt restrain.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Vow and pay to Jehovah your God: Let all who are round about him bring a present to the terrible one.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.x-p15"></a><b>12 </b>He will cut off the spirit of princes: <i>He</i> <i>is</i> terrible to the kings of the earth.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p2"></a>PSALM 77</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician upon Jeduthun. A Psalm of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>My voice [<i>I lifted up</i>] to God, and I cried; My voice [<i>I lifted up</i>] to God, and he heard me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>In the day of my affliction the Lord I sought: My hand in the night was stretched out and relaxed not; Refuse consolation did my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>I will remember God, and will be disquieted; I will meditate, and oppressed with sorrow shall be my spirit. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Thou hast held the watches of my eyes: I am troubled, and will not speak.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p8"></a><b>5 </b>I have recounted the days of old, The years of ages past.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>I will call to remembrance my song in the night: With my heart I will meditate, And search diligently shall my spirit.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p10"></a><b>7 </b>For ever will the Lord east off? And will he be favorable no more?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Gone for ever is his mercy? Fail doth his oracle from generation to generation?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Forgotten to be merciful hath God? Hath he shut up in anger his compassions? Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p13"></a><b>10 </b>And I said my disease [<i>is only for a season</i>;] The years of the right hand of the Most High [<i>I will wait for</i>.]</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p14"></a><b>11 </b>I will remember the works of God; Surely I will remember thy wonders from the beginning.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p15"></a><b>12 </b>And I will meditate on all thy works, And on thy doings I will muse.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p16"></a><b>13 </b>O God! in the sanctuary <i>are</i> thy ways: What god <i>is</i> so great as God?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p17"></a><b>14 </b>Thou art the God who doest wonders; Thou hast made known among the peoples thy strength.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p18"></a><b>15 </b>Thou hast redeemed by [<i>thy</i>] arm thy people, The sons of Jacob and Joseph. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p19"></a><b>16 </b>See thee did the waters, O God! see thee did the waters; They were afraid; also tremble did the deeps.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p20"></a><b>17 </b>The clouds poured out waters; The heavens gave forth a voice: Also thine arrows went abroad.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p21"></a><b>18 </b>The voice of thy thunder was in the circuit, The lightnings illumined the world; The earth trembled and was shaken.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p22"></a><b>19 </b>In the sea are thy ways, And thy paths in the great waters; And thy footsteps are not known.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xi-p23"></a><b>20 </b>Thou leadest like sheep thy people By the hand of Moses and Aaron.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p2"></a>PSALM 78</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p3"></a>A lesson of Instruction [of] Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Give ear, O my people! to my law: Incline your ears to the words of my month.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>I will open in a parable my mouth; I will utter enigmas from ancient Sae.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>What we have heard and known, And our’ fathers have related to us,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>We will not conceal from their children to the generation to come, Recounting the praises of Jehovah and his might, And the wonders which he hath done.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>And he established a testimony in, Jacob, And a law he appointed in Israel; For lie commanded our fathers To make them known to their children;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>That the generations to come might know them, <i>That</i> the children to be born might arise, And declare <i>them</i> to their children.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>That they might set in God their hope, And not forget the works of God; But that his commandments they might observe,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>And not be as their fathers, A generation rebellious and provoking; A generation which set not their heart might, And whose spirit was not faithful towards God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>The children of Ephraim, armed [<i>and</i>] shooting with the bow, Were turned back in the day of battle.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>They kept not the covenant of God, And in his law they refused to walk.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>And they forget his works, And the wonders which he had shown them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>In the sight of their fathers he wrought marvelously; In the land of Egypt, in the field of Zoan.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p16"></a><b>13 </b>He divided the sea, and caused them to pass through, And made the waters to stand as an heap.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p17"></a><b>14 </b>And he led them by a cloud in the day; And all the night by the light of fire.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p18"></a><b>15 </b>He clave the rocks in the wilderness, And made them to drink in great deeps.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p19"></a><b>16 </b>And he brought forth streams from the rock, And made the waters to descend like rivers.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p20"></a><b>17 </b>Yet they continued still to sin against him, To provoke the Most High in the wilderness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p21"></a><b>18 </b>And they tempted God in their heart, By asking food for their soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p22"></a><b>19 </b>And they spake against God: They said, “Can God prepare a table in the wilderness?”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p23"></a><b>20 </b>Behold! he smote the reek, and gush out did the waters; And rivers overflowed. “Can he give bread also? “Will he prepare flesh for his people?”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p24"></a><b>21 </b>Therefore Jehovah heard and was wroth: And a fire was kindled in Jacob: And wrath also ascended against Israel;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p25"></a><b>22 </b>Because they believed not in God, And trusted not in his salvation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p26"></a><b>23 </b>But he had commanded the clouds from above, And the doors of heaven he had opened,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p27"></a><b>24 </b>And had rained down upon them manna for food, And the corn of heaven he had given them:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p28"></a><b>25 </b>The bread of the mighty ones man had eaten: Meat he had sent them to the full.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p29"></a><b>26 </b>He caused to blow an east wind in the heavens; And he raised up by his power the south wind.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p30"></a><b>27 </b>And he rained upon them flesh as dust, And as the sand of the sea leathered fowl;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p31"></a><b>28 </b>And he caused <i>it</i> to fall in the midst of his camp, Round about his tabernacles.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p32"></a><b>29 </b>And they did eat and were filled exceedingly, And their desire he brought to them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p33"></a><b>30 </b>They were not estranged from their desire: The meat was still in their mouth,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p34"></a><b>31 </b>When the wrath of God ascended against them, And slew their fat ones, And brought low the chosen of Israel.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p35"></a><b>32 </b>In all these <i>things</i> they sinned still, And believed not his wonders.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p36"></a><b>33 </b>And he consumed in vanity their days, And their years in haste.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p37"></a><b>34 </b>When he slew them, they sought him; They returned, and hastened early to God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p38"></a><b>35 </b>And they remembered that God was their Rock, And <i>that</i> the Most High God was their Redeemer.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p39"></a><b>36 </b>And they flattered [<i>him</i>] with their mouth, And with their tongue they lied to him:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p40"></a><b>37 </b>But their heart was not right before him, And they were not faithful in his covenant.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p41"></a><b>38 </b>Yet he <i>who</i> <i>is</i> compassionate expiated their iniquity, And did not destroy them: And he multiplied to turn away his anger, And did not stir up all his indignation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p42"></a><b>39 </b>And he remembered that they were flesh; A breath that passeth, and returneth not.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p43"></a><b>40 </b>How often did they provoke him in the desert, [<i>And</i>] grieve him in the wilderness!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p44"></a><b>41 </b>And they returned and tempted God, And the Holy One of Israel they limited.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p45"></a><b>42 </b>They remembered not his hand In the day that he redeemed them from the oppressor,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p46"></a><b>43 </b>When he set in Egypt his signs, And his miracles in the field of Zoan.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p47"></a><b>44 </b>When he turned into blood their rivers; And their streams, that they might not drink of them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p48"></a><b>45 </b>He sent among them a mixture which devoured them; And the frog which destroyed them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p49"></a><b>46 </b>And he gave to the caterpillar their fruit; And their labors to the locusts.   				 <a name="fr_347"></a><a href="#fn_347"><font size="1">348</font></a>
 </p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p51"></a><b>47 </b>And he destroyed with hail their vine, And their wild fig-trees with hailstones.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p52"></a><b>48 </b>And he gave lip to the hail their cattle, And their flocks to thunderbolts.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p53"></a><b>49 </b>He sent upon them the fierceness of his wrath, Fury, anger, and affliction, A mission of evil angels.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p54"></a><b>50 </b>He made a path for his anger: He kept not from death their soul, And their cattle to the pestilence he shut up.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p55"></a><b>51 </b>And he smote all the firstborn in Egypt: The beginning of [<i>their</i>] strength in the tents of Ham.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p56"></a><b>52 </b>And he made to go forth like sheep his people, And led them like a flock in the wilderness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p57"></a><b>53 </b>And he conducted <i>them</i> in safety, and they were not afraid: And their enemies cover did the sea.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p58"></a><b>54 </b>And he brought them to the border of his holiness, This mountain, <i>which</i> his right hand acquired.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p59"></a><b>55 </b>And he expelled from before their face the heathen; And made them to fall into the lot of all inheritance; And caused to dwell in their tents the children of Israel.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p60"></a><b>56 </b>But they tempted and provoked God Most High, And his testimonies they kept not.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p61"></a><b>57 </b>And they turned back and dealt perfidiously like their fathers: They started aside like a bow that is deceitful.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p62"></a><b>58 </b>And they provoked him to anger with their high places; And with their graven images they moved him to anger.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p63"></a><b>59 </b>Hear it did God, and was wroth, And he abhorred exceedingly Israel.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p64"></a><b>60 </b>And he forsook the habitation of Shiloh, The tabernacle where he dwelt among men.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p65"></a><b>61 </b>And he gave into captivity his strength, And his beauty into the hand of the enemy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p66"></a><b>62 </b>And he shut up to the sword his people, And with his own inheritance was wroth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p67"></a><b>63 </b>Their chosen devour did the fire, And their virgins were not applauded.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p68"></a><b>64 </b>Their priests by the sword did fall; And their widows made no lamentation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p69"></a><b>65 </b>But the Lord awoke as one asleep, As a mighty man who crieth out by reason of wine.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p70"></a><b>66 </b>And he smote his enemies behind; Everlasting disgrace he put upon them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p71"></a><b>67 </b>And he rejected the tabernacle of Joseph, And the tribe of Ephraim he chose not:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p72"></a><b>68 </b>But he chose the tribe of Judah, The mountain of Zion, which lie loved:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p73"></a><b>69 </b>And built like high places his sanctuary, Like the earth which he hath founded for ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p74"></a><b>70 </b>And he chose David his servant, And took him from the folds of sheep:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p75"></a><b>71 </b>From following the suckling ewes he took him, To feed Jacob his people, And Israel his inheritance:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p76"></a><b>72 </b>And he fed them in the integrity of his heart, And by the prudence of his hands he guided there.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xiii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p2"></a>PSALM 79</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p3"></a>A Psalm of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O God! come have the heathen into thy inheritance; They have polluted the temple of thy holiness; They have laid Jerusalem in heaps. [fowls of the heavens;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>They have given the dead bodies of thy servants for food to the fowls of the heavens; The flesh of thy meek ones to the beasts of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>They have shed their blood like water around Jerusalem: And there was not <i>one</i> to bury <i>them</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>We have been a reproach to our neighbors; A scorn and a derision to those who are around us.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>How long, O Jehovah! wilt thou be wroth for ever? Burn like fire shall thy jealousy?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Pour out thy wrath upon the heathen who have not known thee, And upon the kingdoms which upon thy name do not call:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>For they have devoured Jacob, And his dwelling they have laid waste.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Remember not against us former iniquities: Make haste, let thy compassions prevent us; For we are afflicted exceedingly.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Help us, O God of our salvation! for the glory of thy name; And deliver us, and be merciful to our sins, for the sake of thy name.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Wherefore should the heathen say, “Where is their God?” Let be made known among the heathen in our sight The vengeance of the blood of thy servants which is shed.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Let the sighing of the prisoner come before thy face: According to the greatness of thy arm, Reserve the children of death:   				 <a name="fr_348"></a><a href="#fn_348"><font size="1">349</font></a>
 </p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p16"></a><b>12 </b>And recompense our neighbors sevenfold into their bosom, Their reproach with which they have reproached thee, O Jehovah!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p17"></a><b>13 </b>And we thy people, and the sheep of thy pastures, Will confess to thee for ever; From generation to generation declaring thy praise.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xiv"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p2"></a>PSALM 80</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician upon Shoshannim Eduth. A Psalm of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O Shepherd of Israel, give ear! Who leadest Joseph like a flock; Thou who sittest between the cherubim, shine forth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Before Ephraim, and Benjamin, and Manasseh, Stir up thy strength, and come for our salvation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Turn us again, O God! and cause to shine thy face, And we shall be safe.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p7"></a><b>4 </b>O Jehovah God of armies! How long wilt thou be incensed against the prayer of thy people?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Thou hast fed us with bread of tears; And hast given us tears to drink in great measure.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Thou hast made us a strife to our neighbors: And our enemies laugh <i>at us</i> among themselves.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p10"></a><b>7 </b>O God of armies! turn us again, And cause to shine thy face upon us, And we shall be safe.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p11"></a><b>8 </b>A vine out of Egypt thou hast brought: Thou hast expelled the heathen, and planted it,.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Thou hast cleansed <i>the ground</i> before it: Thou hast rooted its roots, And it hath filled the land.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Covered were the mountains with its shadow, And its branches <i>were like</i> the cedars of God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p14"></a><b>11 </b>It sent forth its branches to the sea, And to the river its shoots.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Why then hast thou broken down its hedges, So that tear it in pieces do all who pass by the way?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Wasted it hath the boar out of the forest; And the wild beast of the field hath eaten it up.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p17"></a><b>14 </b>O God of armies! return, I beseech <i>thee</i>, Look down from heaven, and behold, And visit this vine,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p18"></a><b>15 </b>And the vineyard which planted hath thy right hand, And [<i>look</i>] upon the shoot   				 <a name="fr_349"></a><a href="#fn_349"><font size="1">350</font></a>
  				 <i>which</i> thou hast strengthened for thyself.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p20"></a><b>16 </b>It is burnt with fire; it is cut down; At the rebuke of thy countenance they perish.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p21"></a><b>17 </b>Let thy hand be upon the Man of thy right hand, Upon the son of man whom thou hast strengthened for thyself,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p22"></a><b>18 </b>And we will not go back from thee: Thou shalt quicken us, and upon thy name we will call.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p23"></a><b>19 </b>O Jehovah, God of armies! turn us again; Cause to shine thy face, And we shall be safe.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xv"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p2"></a>PSALM 81</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician upon Gittith. Of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Exult to God our strength: Shout for joy to the God of Jacob.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Take a song, and bring forth the timbrel, The harp of pleasantness with the nablum.   				 <a name="fr_350"></a><a href="#fn_350"><font size="1">351</font></a>
 </p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p7"></a><b>3 </b>Sound the trumpet   				 <a name="fr_351"></a><a href="#fn_351"><font size="1">352</font></a>
  				 at the new moon; At the time appointed on the day of our sacrifice.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p9"></a><b>4 </b>For a statute to Israel <i>is</i> this, A judgment to the God of Jacob.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p10"></a><b>5 </b>For a testimony in Joseph he set it, When he went forth over the land of Egypt! A language which I understood not I heard.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p11"></a><b>6 </b>“I removed from the burden his shoulder: “His hands from the pots were removed.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p12"></a><b>7 </b>“In trouble thou didst cry, and I rescued thee: “I answered thee in the secret place of thunder: “I proved thee at the waters of Meribah. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p13"></a><b>8 </b>“Hear, O my people! and I will protest to thee: “O Israel! if thou wilt hearken to me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p14"></a><b>9 </b>“Let there not be in thee a strange god: “Neither worship thou a foreign god.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p15"></a><b>10 </b>“I <i>am</i> Jehovah thy God, “Who brought thee out of the land of Egypt: “Open wide thy mouth, and I will fill it.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p16"></a><b>11 </b>“But my people hearkened not to my voice, “And Israel would have none of me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p17"></a><b>12 </b>“And I gave them up to the hardness of their heart: “They shall walk in their own counsels.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p18"></a><b>13 </b>“O if my people had hearkened to me! “<i>If</i> Israel in my ways had walked!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p19"></a><b>14 </b>“Soon their enemies I would have brought low, “And against their adversaries I would have turned my hand:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p20"></a><b>15 </b>“The haters of Jehovah would have lied to him, “And their time should have been for ever:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p21"></a><b>16 </b>“And I would have fed them with the fat of corn: “And from the rock with honey I would have satisfied thee.”</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xvi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p2"></a>PSALM 82</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p3"></a>A Psalm of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>God sitteth in the assembly of God: In the midst of the gods he will judge.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>How long will ye judge unjustly? And the faces of the ungodly will ye lift up? Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Judge the poor and the orphan; The helpless and the destitute justify ye.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Rescue the poor one and the afflicted one: From the hand of the ungodly ones deliver <i>them</i></p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p8"></a><b>5 </b><i>But</i> they know not, neither do they understand <i>any thing</i>: In darkness they walk, <i>Although</i> moved are all the foundations of the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>As for me, I have said, “Ye are gods, “And children of the Most High all of you:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p10"></a><b>7 </b>“Surely as a man ye shall die; “And as one [<i>of the people</i>,] O princes! ye shall fall.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvi-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Arise, O God! judge the earth: For thou shalt inherit all nations.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xvii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p2"></a>PSALM 83</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p3"></a>A Song [or] Psalm, of Asaph</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O God! keep not silence with thyself; Hold not thy peace, and be not still, O God!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>For behold! thy enemies make a tumult: And those who hate thee have lifted up the head.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Against thy people they have craftily formed a design, And have consulted against thy hidden ones.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>They have said, “Come and let us cut them off from being a nation; “And let there be no remembrance of the name of Israel any more.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>For they have consulted with the heart together; Against thee a covenant they have made.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>The tents of Edom, and of the Ishmaelites; Of Moab and of the Hagarenes.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Gebal, and Ammon, and Amalek; The Philistines with the inhabitants of Tyre.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Also Assur is associated with them: They have been an arm to the sons of Lot. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Do to them as to the Midianites, As to Sisera, as to Jabin, at the brook Kishon.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>They perished at Endor; They became manure for the earth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Make them, [<i>even</i>] their princes, like Oreb, and like Zeeb; And like Zebah, and like Zalmunna, all their princes.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Who have said, “Let us take in possession for ourselves “The habitations of God.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p16"></a><b>13 </b>O my God! make them like a whirling ball; Like stubble before the wind.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p17"></a><b>14 </b>As fire burneth a forest, And as the flame kindleth the mountains,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p18"></a><b>15 </b>So pursue them with thy tempest, And with thy whirlwind terrify them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p19"></a><b>16 </b>Fill their faces with shame; That they may seek thy name, O Jehovah!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p20"></a><b>17 </b>Let them be ashamed, and terrified for ever;   				 <a name="fr_352"></a><a href="#fn_352"><font size="1">353</font></a>
  				 And let them be confounded, and perish.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p22"></a><b>18 </b>And let them know that thou, even thou, art, thy name Jehovah, Thou alone the Most High over all the earth.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xviii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p2"></a>PSALM 84</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p3"></a>To The Chief Musician Upon Gittith. A Psalm of the sons of Korah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>How amiable are thy tabernacles, O Jehovah of armies!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Long, yea, even faint doth my soul after the courts of Jehovah: My heart and my flesh leap for joy towards the living God.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Also the sparrow hath found a house for herself, And the swallow a nest for herself, Where she may place her young ones: O thine altars! thou Jehovah of armies! my King and my God!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Blessed <i>are</i> those who dwell in thy house: Continually they will be praising thee. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Blessed <i>is</i> the man whose strength is in thee; The ways [<i>are</i>] in their heart.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>They passing through the valley of weeping, will together make it a fountain; Also the cisterns the rain will cover.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>They will journey from strength to strength; Seen will be the God of gods in Zion.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>O Jehovah, God of armies! hear my prayer: Hearken, O God of Jacob! Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Our shield do thou behold, O God! And look upon the face of thy Christ.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>For better is one day in thy courts than a thousand elsewhere. I would rather be a doorkeeper in the house of my God, Than dwell in the tents of ungodliness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>For a sun and shield <i>is</i> Jehovah God <i>to us</i>; Grace and glory give will Jehovah; He will not withhold <i>any</i> good from those who walk uprightly.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xviii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>O Jehovah of armies! Blessed <i>is</i> the man who confideth in thee.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xix"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p2"></a>PSALM 85</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p3"></a>To the Chief Musician. A Psalm of the sons of Korah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Thou hast been favorable, O Jehovah! to thy land: Thou hast brought back the captivity of Jacob.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Thou hast taken away the iniquity of thy people: Thou hast covered all their sins. Selah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Thou hast turned away all thy anger: Thou hast drawn back the fury of thy indignation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Turn us, O God of our salvation! And relax thy anger against us.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Wilt thou for ever be angry with us? Wilt thou prolong thy wrath from age to age?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Wilt not thou being turned <i>to us</i> quicken us? And thy people will rejoice in thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Show us, O Jehovah! thy mercy; and thy salvation grant unto us.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p11"></a><b>8 </b>I will hear what God Jehovah will speak: Surely he will speak peace to his people and to his meek ones, And they will not return to folly.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Surely near to those who fear him is his salvation, That dwell may glory in our land.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Mercy and truth shall meet together; Righteousness and peace shall kiss [<i>each other</i>.]</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Truth out of the earth shall spring up; And righteousness from heaven shall look down.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Likewise Jehovah will give that which is good: And our land shall yield her increase.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xix-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Righteousness before him shall go; And shall set in the way her steps.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xx"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p2"></a>PSALM 86</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p3"></a>A Prayer of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Incline, O Jehovah, thy ear, answer me; For poor and needy <i>am</i> I.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Keep my soul, for I am meek: O thou, my God! save thy servant who trusteth in thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Have compassion upon me, O Jehovah! For to thee do I cry daily.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Gladden the soul of thy servant; For to thee, O Lord! my soul I lift up.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p8"></a><b>5 </b>For thou, O Lord! <i>art</i> good, and gracious, Plenteous in mercy to all who call upon thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Listen, O Jehovah! to my prayer, Attend to the voice of my supplications.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p10"></a><b>7 </b>In the day of my trouble I will cry to thee: For thou wilt answer me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p11"></a><b>8 </b>There is none like unto thee, O Lord! among the gods; And <i>there</i> is none [<i>who can work</i>] according to thy works.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p12"></a><b>9 </b>All the nations which thou hast made shall come, And shall worship before thy face, O Lord! And glory they shall give to thy name:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p13"></a><b>10 </b>For great art thou, And doing wonders, thou God alone.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Show me, O Jehovah! thy ways; I will walk in thy truth: Unite my heart to fear thy name.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p15"></a><b>12 </b>I will celebrate thee, O Lord my God! with my whole heart; And I will glorify thy name for ever;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p16"></a><b>13 </b>For thy mercy hath been great towards me; And thou hast delivered my soul from the lower grave.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p17"></a><b>14 </b>O God! the proud have risen up against me, And a company of mighty men have sought after my soul; And they have not set thee before them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p18"></a><b>15 </b>And thou, O Lord! [<i>art</i>] a God compassionate and gracious; Slow to anger; and plenteous in mercy and truth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p19"></a><b>16 </b>Look to me, and have pity upon me: Give thy strength to thy servant, And save the son of thy handmaid.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xx-p20"></a><b>17 </b>Make with me a sign for good: And see shall my adversaries and be ashamed; For thou, O Jehovah! hast secured me and comforted me.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xxi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p2"></a>PSALM 87</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p3"></a>A Psalm [or] Song of the sons of Korah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>His foundations [<i>are</i>] in the holy mountains.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Love doth Jehovah the gates of Zion More than all the tabernacles of Jacob.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Glorious things are spoken of thee, O city of God! Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>I will make mention of Rahab, and Babel among those who know me: Behold the Philistines, and Tyre, with Ethiopia, He is born there! Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p8"></a><b>5 </b>And of Zion it shall be said, “Man and man is born in her; “And the Most High himself will establish her.”</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>The Lord will recount when he writeth the peoples, “He is born there.” Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxi-p10"></a><b>7 </b>And the singers as the players upon instruments: All my springs <i>are</i> in thee.</p>  <a name="xxxv.iii.xxii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p2"></a>PSALM 88</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p3"></a>A Song of a Psalm of the sons of Korah. To the Chief Musician, upon Machalath, to make humble. An instruction of Heman the Ezrahite</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O Jehovah! God of my salvation! By day I cry, by night before thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Come into thy presence let my prayer; Incline thy ear to my cry;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>For filled with troubles is my soul; And my life to hell   				 <a name="fr_353"></a><a href="#fn_353"><font size="1">354</font></a>
  				 hath drawn near.</p>
