 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Sharpened have they their tongue like a serpent: The poison of an asp is under their lips. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Keep me, O Jehovah! from the hands of the ungodly: From the man of injuries preserve me; Who plot to overthrow my goings.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Laid have the proud a snare for me: And with cords they have spread a net: By the wayside traps have they set for me. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>I said, O Jehovah! my God are thou: Listen, O Jehovah! to the voice of my supplication.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>O Jehovah, my Lord! the strength of my salvation, Thou hast put a covering on my head in the day of arms.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Grant not, O Jehovah! the desires of the ungodly man: They have devised, consummate thou not, they shall be exalted. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>[<i>As for</i>] the head of those who encompass me, Let the mischief of his lips cover him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Fall upon them let coals with fire: He shall cast them into deep pits, They shall not rise again.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>The man of tongue shall not be established in the earth: The man of violence, evil shall hunt him to banishments.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>I have known that accomplish will Jehovah the judgment of the poor one, The judgment of the afflicted one.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxii-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Surely the righteous ones will celebrate thy name, Dwell shall the upright ones before thy face.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxiii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p2"></a>PSALM 141</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p3"></a>A Psalm of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O Jehovah! I have cried to thee: Haste thou to me: Listen to my voice when I cry to thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Directed let my prayer be as incense before thy face: [<i>Let</i>] the lifting up of my hands [<i>be</i>] as the sacrifice of the evening.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Set, O Jehovah! a watch to my mouth; Keep a guard upon the door of my lips.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Incline not my heart to an evil thing, To commit works of ungodliness with the men who work iniquity; And let me not eat of their dainties.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Smite me let the righteous man, [<i>it shall be</i>] a kindness; And let him chastise me, [<i>it shall be</i>] an oil that is precious, It shall not break my head: For yet also my prayer <i>shall be</i> in their calamities.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Cast down on stony places have been their judges: And they shall hear my words, for they are sweet.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>As he who breaketh and cutteth on the earth, Scattered have been our bones at the mouth of the grave.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Because to thee, O Jehovah! my Lord! <i>are</i> my eyes, In thee I have hoped: do not leave destitute my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Keep me from the hands of the snare which they have spread for me. From the nets of those who work iniquity.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Fall into his nets let the ungodly ones together, Until I escape.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxiv"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p2"></a>PSALM 142</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p3"></a>Maschil of David, when he was in the cave. A Prayer</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p4"></a><b>1</b> With my voice to, Jehovah I cried; With my voice to. Jehovah I made supplication.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p5"></a><b>2 </b>I poured out before his face my meditation; My affliction before his face I declare.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p6"></a><b>3 </b>When perplexed within me was my spirit, And thou knewest my path: In the way wherein I walked, they laid a snare for me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p7"></a><b>4 </b>On looking to the right hand, and beholding, None there was who would know me, Perish did refuge from me, [<i>There was</i>] no man seeking after my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p8"></a><b>5 </b>I cried to thee, O Jehovah! I said, Thou <i>art</i> my hope, My portion in the land of the living.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Attend to my cry, For under affliction I labor exceedingly: Deliver me from my persecutors, For they are too strong for me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxiv-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Rescue from prison my soul, That I may celebrate thy name: Crown me shall the righteous ones, For thou shalt recompense me.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxv"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p2"></a>PSALM 143</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p3"></a>A Psalm of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p4"></a><b>1 </b>O Jehovah! hear my prayer; Give ear to my supplication; In thy truth answer me, in thy righteousness.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p5"></a><b>2 </b>And enter not into judgment with thy servant, For there shall not be justified in thy sight any living man.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p6"></a><b>3 </b>For persecuted hath the enemy my soul; He hath prostrated on the earth my life; He hath set me in dark <i>places</i>, as the dead of an age.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p7"></a><b>4 </b>And perplexed within me is my spirit Within me astonished is my heart.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p8"></a><b>5 </b>I remembered the days of old, I meditated on all thy doings; Upon the work of thy hands I meditated.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p9"></a><b>6 </b>I spread out my hearts to thee; My soul, as the earth without water, <i>is</i> to thee. Selah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Hasten, answer me, O Jehovah! Fail doth my spirit: Hide not thy face from me, Because I shall be like to those who descend into the pit.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Cause me to hear in the morning thy mercy, For in thee have I hoped: Show me the way in which I may walk, For to thee have I lifted up my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Deliver me from my enemies, O Jehovah! With thee have I hidden [<i>myself</i>.]</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Teach me to do thy will, For thou <i>art</i> my God: Let thy good Spirit lead me into the right land.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Because of thy name, O Jehovah I thou wilt quicken me: In thy righteousness bring out of trouble my soul.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxv-p15"></a><b>12 </b>And in thy mercy thou wilt scatter my enemies, And wilt destroy all those who afflict my soul; Because I <i>am</i> thy servant.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxvi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p2"></a>PSALM 144</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p3"></a>Of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Blessed <i>be</i> Jehovah, my strength, Who teacheth my hands for the fight, My fingers for the battle.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>My goodness, and my fortress, My citadel, my deliverer for me, My shield, and in him I have hoped, Who subdueth my people under me.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>O Jehovah! what is man that thou acknowledgest him? The son of man that thou thinkest of him?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Man to vanity is like, His days [<i>are</i>] as a shadow that is passing.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p8"></a><b>5 </b>O Jehovah! bow thy heavens and descend: Touch the mountains and they shall smoke.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Thunder forth thunderings and scatter them; Shoot out thy arrows, and destroy them.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Send thy hand from on high; Rescue me and deliver me from waters great, From the hand of the sons of the alien.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p11"></a><b>8 </b>For their mouth hath spoken falsehood, And their right hand is a right hand of deceit.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p12"></a><b>9 </b>O God! a song that is new I will sing to thee: Upon the nablum, upon the psaltery I will sing psalms to thee</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Who givest salvation to kings, Who redeemest David his servant from the hurtful sword.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Redeem me, and rescue me, From the hand of the sons of the alien, Whose mouth hath spoken falsehood, And their right hand <i>is</i> a right hand of deceit.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Because our sons <i>are</i> as plants Which have grown up in their youth; Our daughters as corners polished After the similitude of a palace.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Our recesses full, Supplying all kinds of good things. Our sheep bringing forth thousands, [<i>Yea</i>] ten thousands in our streets.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p17"></a><b>14 </b>Our oxen to the burden accustomed; No breach, nor going out, Nor cry in our streets.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvi-p18"></a><b>15 </b>Happy the people to whom it is so, To whom Jehovah is their God.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxvii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p2"></a>PSALM 145</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p3"></a>Praise of David</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>I will exalt thee, my God, <i>my</i> King! And will bless thy name for ever and ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Every day will I bless thee, And praise thy name for ever and ever.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Great <i>is</i> Jehovah, and to be praised greatly, And his greatness is incomprehensible.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Generation to generation shall praise thy works, And thy power they shall declare.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Upon the majesty of the glory of thy excellence, And upon the words of thy wonders, I will meditate.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>And the might of thy terrible <i>works</i> shall they recount; And thy greatness I will declare.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>The memory of the greatness of thy goodness they shall speak forth; And of thy righteousness they shall sing.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Gracious and compassionate <i>is</i> Jehovah, Slow to anger and great in clemency.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Good <i>is</i> Jehovah to all, And his compassions <i>are</i> over all his works.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Celebrate thee, O Jehovah! shall all thy works, And thy meek ones shall bless thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Of the glory of thy kingdom they shall tell, And of thy power they shall speak:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p15"></a><b>12 </b>To make known to the sons of men his mighty acts, And the glory of the beauty of his kingdom.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Thy kingdom <i>is</i> a kingdom of all ages, And thy dominion is throughout generations of generations.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p17"></a><b>14 </b>Uphold doth Jehovah all the falling, He raiseth up all who are bowed down.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p18"></a><b>15 </b>The eyes of all in thee do hope, And thou givest them their food in its season.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p19"></a><b>16 </b>Thou openest thy hand And satisfiest every living <i>creature</i> by thy good pleasure.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p20"></a><b>17 </b>Righteous <i>is</i> Jehovah in all his ways, And merciful in all his works.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p21"></a><b>18 </b>Near <i>is</i> Jehovah to all who call upon him, To all who call upon him in truth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p22"></a><b>19 </b>The desire of those who fear him he will perform, And their cry he will hear, told he will save then,.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p23"></a><b>20 </b>Keep doth Jehovah all who love him, And all the wicked he will destroy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxvii-p24"></a><b>21 </b>The praise of Jehovah speak shall my mouth: And bless shall all flesh his holy name for ever and ever.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxviii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p2"></a>PSALM 146</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p3"></a>Hallelujah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Praise, O my soul! Jehovah.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>I will praise Jehovah in my life; I will sing psalms to my God, while I have being.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Confide not in princes, <i>Nor</i> in the son of man, in whom there is not help.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Go forth shall his breath, He shall return to his earth, In that day perish shall his thoughts.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Blessed <i>is</i> he who hath for his help the God of Jacob; Whose hope is in Jehovah, his God:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Who made heaven and earth, The sea, and all that is in them: Who keepeth truth for ever:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Who doeth judgment for those who are unrighteously oppressed: Who giveth bread to the hungry: Jehovah looseth the prisoners;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Jehovah enlighteneth the blind; Jehovah raiseth up those who are bowed down; Jehovah loveth the righteous;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Jehovah keepeth the strangers; The orphan and the widow he succoureth; And the way of the ungodly he will destroy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxviii-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Reign shall Jehovah for ever: Thy God, O Zion, <i>is</i> from generation to generation. Hallelujah.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxix"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p2"></a>PSALM 147</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p3"></a><b>1 </b>Praise ye God; For it is a good <i>thing</i> to sing psalms to our God, For<i> it is</i> pleasant, comely <i>is</i> praise.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p4"></a><b>2 </b>Build up Jerusalem doth Jehovah, The dispersed of Israel he will gather.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p5"></a><b>3 </b>He healeth the contrite in heart; He bindeth their sorrows.   				 <a name="fr_403"></a><a href="#fn_403"><font size="1">404</font></a>
 </p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p7"></a><b>4 </b>He counteth the multitude of the stars: To each of them names doth he give.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Great is our Lord, and abundant in power, His understanding is infinite.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p9"></a><b>6 </b>Raise up the afflicted ones doth Jehovah, He casteth down the ungodly ones to the ground.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Sing to Jehovah in praise, Sing psalms to our God upon the harp.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Who covereth the heavens with clouds, Who prepareth for the earth rain, Who maketh to spring up grass upon the mountains,</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Who giveth to the cattle their food, To the young ones   				 <a name="fr_404"></a><a href="#fn_404"><font size="1">405</font></a>
  				 of the ravens which cry to him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p15"></a><b>10 </b>Nor in the strength of the horse will he take pleasure, Nor in the legs of man will he delight.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p16"></a><b>11 </b>Delight doth Jehovah in those who fear him, [<i>In those</i>] who hope in his mercy.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p17"></a><b>12 </b>Celebrate, O Jerusalem! Jehovah; Praise thy God, O Zion!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p18"></a><b>13 </b>For he strengtheneth the bars of thy gates; He blesseth thy children in the midst of thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p19"></a><b>14 </b>Who maketh in thy borders peace; With the fatness of wheat he satisfieth thee.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p20"></a><b>15 </b>When he sendeth forth his word upon the earth, Very swiftly run doth his word.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p21"></a><b>16 </b>Who giveth snow <i>white</i> as wool; The hoarfrost as ashes he scattereth.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p22"></a><b>17 </b>He casteth forth his ice as morsels: Before his cold who shall stand?</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p23"></a><b>18 </b>He shall send his word: red shall melt them: Blow shall his breath, <i>and</i> flow shall the waters.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p24"></a><b>19 </b>He announceth his words to Jacob, his statutes and his judgments to Israel.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxix-p25"></a><b>20 </b>He hath not done so to every nation, And his judgments he hath not made known to them. Hallelujah.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxx"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p2"></a>PSALM 148</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p3"></a>Hallelujah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Praise ye Jehovah from the heavens; Praise him in the heights.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Praise him, all ye his angels! Praise him, all ye his armies!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Praise him, ye Sun and Moon! Praise him, all ye shining stars!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p7"></a><b>4 </b>Praise him, ye heavens of heavens! And ye waters above the heavens!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Let them praise the name of Jehovah; For he commanded and they were created:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p9"></a><b>6 </b>And he established them for ever: For ever he hath set for them a decree, and it shall not pass beyond.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p10"></a><b>7 </b>Praise Jehovah, ye <i>creatures</i> from the earth! Dragons, and all deeps!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p11"></a><b>8 </b>Fire and hail, snow and ice! Wind of storm, executing his word!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p12"></a><b>9 </b>Mountains, and all hills! The tree bearing fruit, and all cedars!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p13"></a><b>10 </b>Wild beasts, and all cattle! Reptile, and winged birds!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p14"></a><b>11 </b>Kings of the earth, and all peoples! Princes, and all judges of the earth!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p15"></a><b>12 </b>Young men, and also maidens! Old men with children!</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p16"></a><b>13 </b>Let them praise the name of Jehovah; For high is his name alone; His praise is above the earth and heavens.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxx-p17"></a><b>14 </b>And he hath exalted the horn of his people: Praise <i>is</i> to all his merciful ones, To the children of Israel, A people which is near to him. Hallelujah.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxxi"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p2"></a>PSALM 149</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p3"></a>Hallelujah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Sing ye to Jehovah a song that is new: His praise <i>is</i> in the assembly of the merciful ones.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Rejoice let Israel in his Maker; Let the children of Zion exult in their king:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Let them praise his name on the pipe: On the timbrel and the harp let them sing psalms to him.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p7"></a><b>4 </b>For taken pleasure hath Jehovah in his people: He will glorify the poor ones unto salvation.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Exult let the merciful ones in glory; Let them shout with joy on their couches.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p9"></a><b>6 </b>The exaltations of God are in their mouth, And a sword of two edges in their hand;</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p10"></a><b>7 </b>To execute vengeance on the heathen, Chastisements on the nations:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p11"></a><b>8 </b>To bind their kings with chains, And their nobles with fetters of iron:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxi-p12"></a><b>9 </b>To execute upon them the judgment written. This honor is to all his merciful ones. Hallelujah.</p>  <a name="xxxv.v.xxxii"></a>  			 
 <p class="Normal"><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p1"></a>  			 
 </p><p class="HDG-C-Gr-16-Pref14"><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p2"></a>PSALM 150</p>  			 
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent26"><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p3"></a>Hallelujah</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p4"></a><b>1 </b>Praise God in his sanctuary; Praise him in the firmament of his power.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p5"></a><b>2 </b>Praise him in his might; Praise him for the multitude of his greatness:</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p6"></a><b>3 </b>Praise him with sound of trumpet; Praise him with nablum and harp.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p7"></a><b>4</b> Praise him with timbrel and pipe; Praise him with strings and organ.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p8"></a><b>5 </b>Praise him with cymbals of sound; Praise him with cymbals of shouting.</p>  			 
 <p><a name="xxxv.v.xxxii-p9"></a>6 Let every thing that breatheth praise God. Hallelujah.</p>  
 <hr>

 <p><a name="fn_328"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_328">329</a> <a name="xxxv.ii.xvii-p12.1"></a>

 <p class="Center"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxiv-p18"></a>“And let men know even unto the ends of the earth, <br> 					 That God ruleth in Jacob. Selah.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_335"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_335">336</a> <a name="xxxv.ii.xxvii-p12.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxvii-p13"></a> The free translation of the French version is here adopted.  <p><a name="fn_336"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_336">337</a> <a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p6.1"></a>

 <p><a name="fn_337"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_337">338</a> <a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p10.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxx-p11"></a> In the French version it is “by the power.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_338"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_338">339</a> <a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p9.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p10"></a> That is, the Jordan. See <a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p10.1"></a><a href="../../../bib/kjv/jos004.htm#023">Jos 4:23</a><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p10.1"></a></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_339"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_339">340</a> <a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p11.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p12"></a> “<a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p12.1"></a>Dominatur seculo.” — <i>Lat.</i> “<a name="xxxv.ii.xxxi-p12.2"></a>Il domine sur le monde.” — <i>Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_340"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_340">341</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.v-p20.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p21"></a> Literally, “moreover.” But see the Commentary.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_341"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_341">342</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.v-p25.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.v-p26"></a> “<a name="xxxv.iii.v-p26.1"></a>In organo musico.” — <i>Lat. </i>“<a name="xxxv.iii.v-p26.2"></a>Avec irgyes de musique.” — <i>Fr.</i> The Hebrew is <a name="xxxv.iii.v-p26.3"></a>בכלי-נבל <i>bichli-nebel,</i> “which is the instrument of the nebel, <i>or</i> psaltery.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_342"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_342">343</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p21.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.vi-p22"></a> In the French versions this line reads — “Blessed be the Lord <i>God</i> of Israel, the God of gods.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_343"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_343">344</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p2.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p3"></a> According to the Hebrew division, Part 3 extends from <a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p3.1"></a><a href="../../../bib/kjv/psa073.htm#000">Psalm 73</a><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p3.1"></a> to <a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p3.2"></a><a href="../../../bib/kjv/psa089.htm#000">Psalm 89</a><a name="xxxv.iii.vii-p3.2"></a> inclusive</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_344"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_344">345</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p5.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p6"></a> In French version it is, “which thou hast acquired of old.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_345"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_345">346</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p9.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p10"></a> From the obscurity of the literal translation of the Latin version, the free reading of the French version is adopted in these two lines.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_346"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_346">347</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p18.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.viii-p19"></a> Literally “break.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_347"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_347">348</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p49.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xii-p50"></a> In the French version it is “to the grasshopper.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_348"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_348">349</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p14.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiii-p15"></a> “That is,” says Jebb, “let there be some spared out of those who are marked out for death by their enemies.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_349"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_349">350</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p18.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p19"></a> “Shoot” is the rendering in the French version, the word being “<a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p19.1"></a>provin.” In the Latin version it is “<a name="xxxv.iii.xiv-p19.2"></a>filium,” “son,” the literal translation of the Hebrew text.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_350"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_350">351</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p5.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p6"></a> Psaltery. — <i>Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_351"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_351">352</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p7.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xv-p8"></a> We follow here the French version. In the Latin version, instead of “trumpet” it is “harp,” which is evidently incorrect.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_352"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_352">353</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p20.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xvii-p21"></a> In the French version it is “greatly.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_353"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_353">354</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p6.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p7"></a> “To the grave.” — <i>Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_354"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_354">355</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p8.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxii-p9"></a> “To the pit.” — <i>Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_355"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_355">356</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxiii-p14.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxiii-p15"></a> In the French version it is “thou hast founded.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_356"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_356">357</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxiii-p51.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxiii-p52"></a> Literally, “of what age I am.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_357"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_357">358</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p2.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p3"></a> According to the Hebrew division, Part 4 extends from <a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p3.1"></a><a href="../../../bib/kjv/psa090.htm#000">Psalm 90</a><a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p3.1"></a> to <a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p3.2"></a><a href="../../../bib/kjv/psa106.htm#000">Psalm 106</a><a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p3.2"></a> inclusive.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_358"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_358">359</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p10.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxiv-p11"></a> In the French version it is, “Thou carriest them away as do floods of water.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_359"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_359">360</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxvi-p5.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxvi-p6"></a> In the French version it is “<a name="xxxv.iii.xxvi-p6.1"></a>le manichordion,” which Randle Cotgrave translates “an (old fashioned) Clavicord.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_360"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_360">361</a> <a name="xxxv.iii.xxvi-p6.2"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iii.xxvi-p7"></a> In the French version this line reads, — “With the song upon the harp.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_361"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_361">362</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.i-p4.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.i-p5"></a> “From that time,” that is, from the creation of the world mentioned in the previous verse.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_362"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_362">363</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.i-p5.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.i-p6"></a> In explaining this verse, Calvin expresses his approbation of a translation somewhat different: —</p>  				  
 <p class="PoetryLast-DkBlu-11-Cent05"><a name="xxxv.iv.i-p7"></a>“As from eternity thou art, <br> 					 Even so thy throne hath been erected (or prepared) from that time.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_363"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_363">364</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.i-p9.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.i-p10"></a> “<a name="xxxv.iv.i-p10.1"></a>A vocibus.” — <i>Lat.</i> “<a name="xxxv.iv.i-p10.2"></a>A cause du bruit.” —<i> Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_364"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_364">365</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.viii-p4.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.viii-p5"></a> “<a name="xxxv.iv.viii-p5.1"></a>Exsultate Jehovae.” — <i>Lat.</i> “<a name="xxxv.iv.viii-p5.2"></a>Chanter a haute voix au Seigneur.” — <i>Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_365"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_365">366</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.viii-p8.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.viii-p9"></a> In the French it is “give glory to him.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_366"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_366">367</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.x-p6.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.x-p7"></a> From verse 3d to verse 11th inclusive, the verbs we have rendered in the present tense are in the preterite in the Latin version, but in this instance we follow the French version in which they are in the present.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_367"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_367">368</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.x-p13.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.x-p14"></a> “Tears” — <i>Fr.</i></p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_368"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_368">369</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xiii-p42.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.xiii-p43"></a> In the Commentary, (vol 4, p. 202) we have translated “they asked,” by mistake. Calvin seems to understand this as spoken of God.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_369"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_369">370</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xiv-p43.1"></a>

 <p><a name="fn_374"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_374">375</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xvii-p14.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.xvii-p15"></a> In the French version it is — “And let his children be vagabonds and beg.”</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_375"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_375">376</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xvii-p15.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.iv.xvii-p16"></a> In the French version it is — “And seek [<i>for bread</i>] going out of their waste <i>or</i> ruined dwellings.”</p>

 <p><a name="fn_381"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_381">382</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xxi-p9.1"></a>

 <p><a name="fn_384"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_384">385</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xxiv-p10.1"></a>

 <p><a name="fn_386"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_386">387</a> <a name="xxxv.iv.xxvi-p16.1"></a>

 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.v.i-p68"></a> Here the reading in the Latin text is ambiguous. The above is the reading in the French version; and as determined by Calvin in the Commentary.</p>

 <p><a name="fn_395"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_395">396</a> <a name="xxxv.v.xiii-p5.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.v.xiii-p6"></a> These two lines which are David’s oath are in the abrupt form in which the Jews were accustomed to swear.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_396"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_396">397</a> <a name="xxxv.v.xiv-p8.1"></a>   				  
 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.v.xiv-p9"></a> These two verses have also the abrupt termination characteristic of the Jewish form of swearing.</p> 				
 <p><a name="fn_397"></a><a href="cc12034.htm#fr_397">398</a> <a name="xxxv.v.xv-p5.1"></a>

 </p><p class="Footnote"><a name="xxxv.v.xvii-p20"></a> In the French version the verb for “speak” in this line; and the verbs for “see” and “hear” in the two next lines, are in the present tense.</p>
